**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Data Flow Q&A: Envoy Request Routing

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/envoy--d7809ba2 (mirror of envoyproxy/envoy)
**Task Type:** Data Flow Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Envoy is a high-performance proxy that routes HTTP requests from downstream clients to upstream services. Understanding the complete path from the initial TCP accept through filter processing to the final upstream connection is critical for working with Envoy's architecture.

## Task

Trace the complete path of a single HTTP request from the moment a downstream client TCP connection is accepted through filter chain processing, route resolution, upstream cluster selection, and connection establishment. Identify every key transformation point, component boundary crossing, and state change.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions about Envoy's request routing flow:

### Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain

When a downstream client establishes a TCP connection to Envoy, how does the request travel from socket accept to network filter processing?

- Which component accepts the incoming TCP connection?
- How does Envoy select which network filter chain to apply based on connection properties?
- At what point does the connection get handed to the HTTP Connection Manager (HCM)?
- What triggers the initial `onData()` call when bytes arrive?

### Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration

Once bytes arrive at the HCM, how does Envoy parse HTTP and iterate through filters?

- How does the codec parse the byte stream into HTTP headers/body?
- When is the `ActiveStream` created and how does it relate to filter iteration?
- How does the `FilterManager` determine the order of decoder filter execution?
- What filter return values can stop or continue iteration?

### Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection

When the router filter is invoked, how does it select the upstream destination?

- How does the router determine which route configuration to use?
- What is the sequence of operations that resolves a route entry to a specific upstream cluster?
- How does the router select a specific upstream host from the cluster?
- What triggers the creation of the upstream connection?

### Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow

Once an upstream host is selected, how does Envoy establish the connection and forward the request?

- How does the connection pool provide or create an upstream connection?
- What component actually writes the HTTP request to the upstream socket?
- How does the response flow back from upstream through the filter chain?
- At what points does the encoder filter chain get invoked vs. the decoder filter chain?

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:

```
# Envoy Request Routing Flow

## Q1: Listener Accept to Network Filter Chain
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q2: HTTP Parsing and Filter Chain Iteration
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q3: Route Resolution and Upstream Selection
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Q4: Upstream Connection and Data Flow
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and method references>

## Evidence
<consolidated list of supporting file paths and line references>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT modify any source files
- Cite specific files, classes, and methods — avoid vague or speculative answers
- Focus on the core request path, not error handling or edge cases
- Trace a single successful HTTP/1.1 request without TLS termination

## Investigation Summary

The complete HTTP request routing flow in Envoy spans **7 phases** across **14 key source files**:

### Phase 1 — TCP Accept
- **`TcpListenerImpl::onSocketEvent()`** (`tcp_listener_impl.cc:56`) — libevent fires, `socket_->ioHandle().accept()` performs the kernel `accept(4)` syscall, wraps the fd in `AcceptedSocketImpl`, calls `cb_.onAccept()`
- **`ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()` → `onAcceptWorker()`** (`active_tcp_listener.cc:80,108`) — creates `ActiveTcpSocket`, calls `onSocketAccepted()`
- **`ActiveTcpSocket::continueFilterChain()`** — iterates listener filters (TLS Inspector, HTTP Inspector, etc.), then calls `newConnection()`
- **`ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()`** (`active_stream_listener_base.cc:38`) — calls `findFilterChain()`, `createServerConnection()`, and `createNetworkFilterChain()` to install network filters

### Phase 2 — Filter Chain Selection
- **`FilterChainManagerImpl::findFilterChain()`** (`filter_chain_manager_impl.cc:513`) — matches on destination port → IP → SNI → transport protocol → ALPN in priority order

### Phase 3 — Network Filter Chain / HCM
- **`FilterManagerImpl::onRead()`** (`filter_manager_impl.cc:100`) — iterates `ReadFilter` list, calls `filter->onData()`
- **`ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()`** (`conn_manager_impl.cc:486`) — on first call, `createCodec()` sniffs the protocol and creates the HTTP/1.1 or HTTP/2 codec; then `codec_->dispatch(data)` parses bytes

### Phase 4 — HTTP Stream Creation
- **`ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()`** (`conn_manager_impl.cc:387`) — codec callback; creates `ActiveStream` (owns the HTTP `FilterManager`), adds to `streams_` list

The investigation traced the **complete HTTP request routing flow** in Envoy (`github.com/sg-evals/envoy--d7809ba2`) across all four requested dimensions, with precise file and line references verified directly from the source code:

### What Was Investigated

**Q1 — TCP Accept through Filter Chain Processing**
- `TcpListenerImpl::onSocketEvent()` → `ActiveTcpListener::onAccept()` → `ActiveTcpSocket::continueFilterChain()` → `ActiveStreamListenerBase::newConnection()`

- `FilterManagerImpl::onRead()` → `ConnectionManagerImpl::onData()` → `createCodec()` + `codec_->dispatch()`

**Q2 — HTTP Filter Chain Iteration**
- `ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream()` creates `ActiveStream` with its own `FilterManager`

**Q4 — Connection Pool and Upstream Connection Establishment**
- `UpstreamRequest::acceptHeadersFromRouter()` → `conn_pool_->newStream()`

[notifies UpstreamRequest]\n    [if no ready client]\n      \u2192 newPendingStream()                            [queue the request]\n      \u2192 tryCreateNewConnection()                      conn_pool_base.cc:163\n        \u2192 instantiateActiveClient()                   conn_pool_base.h:180\n          \u2192 Http::ActiveClient()\n            \u2192 host()->createConnection()              [TCP connect()]\n            \u2192 createCodecClient(data)                 [wraps conn in HTTP codec]\n\n[UpstreamCodecFilter::decodeHeaders()]                upstream_codec_filter.cc:52\n  [if upstream ready]\n    \u2192 upstream()->encodeHeaders(headers, end_stream)  [write to upstream codec]\n  [if upstream not ready]\n    \u2192 latch headers; StopAllIterationAndWatermark\n    [on pool ready: onUpstreamConnectionEstablished() flushes latched headers]\n\n[Response path]\n  CodecBridge::decodeHeaders()                        upstream_codec_filter.cc:147\n    \u2192 callbacks_->encodeHeaders()                     [upstream FilterManager]\n      \u2192 UpstreamRequest::decodeHeaders()\n        \u2192 Router::Filter::onUpstreamHeaders()\n          \u2192 callbacks_->encodeHeaders()               [downstream FilterManager]\n            \u2192 downstream codec \u2192 client\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key Design Observations\n\n### 1. Dual Filter Manager Architecture\nEnvoy uses two separate `FilterManager` instances per request:\n- **Downstream `FilterManager`** (inside `ActiveStream`): processes the request from client to router, and the response from router to client.\n- **Upstream `FilterManager`** (`UpstreamFilterManager` inside `UpstreamRequest`): processes the request from router to upstream codec, and the response from upstream codec back to the router.\n\nThe `UpstreamCodecFilter` is the terminal filter in the upstream chain, bridging the upstream `FilterManager` to the actual `GenericUpstream` (codec).\n\n### 2. Connection Pool Decoupling\n`conn_pool_->newStream(this)` is called in `acceptHeadersFromRouter()` **before** `filter_manager_->decodeHeaders()`. This means the TCP connection to the upstream is initiated as early as possible, while upstream HTTP filters are still processing the request headers. If the connection is not yet ready when `UpstreamCodecFilter::decodeHeaders()` runs, headers are latched and flushed via `onUpstreamConnectionEstablished()`.\n\n### 3. Synchronous vs. Asynchronous Host Selection\n`cluster->chooseHost()` returns a `HostSelectionResponse` that may include a `cancelable` handle. If the runtime feature `envoy.reloadable_features.async_host_selection` is enabled and the load balancer supports it, host selection is deferred and the filter chain returns `StopAllIterationAndWatermark`. The `on_host_selected_` callback resumes the chain when the host is resolved.\n\n### 4. Filter Chain Selection Specificity\n`findFilterChainUsingMatcher()` evaluates criteria from most-specific (port + IP + SNI + transport + ALPN) to least-specific. The first matching chain wins. This allows a single listener to serve both plaintext HTTP/1.1 and TLS HTTP/2 on the same port by differentiating on transport protocol and ALPN.\n\n### 5. Network vs. HTTP Filter Managers\nThe **network-level** `FilterManagerImpl` (`source/common/network/filter_manager_impl.cc`) manages `ReadFilter`/`WriteFilter` objects operating on raw byte buffers. The **HTTP-level** `FilterManager` (`source/common/http/filter_manager.cc`) manages `StreamDecoderFilter`/`StreamEncoderFilter` objects operating on parsed HTTP frames. The HCM (`ConnectionManagerImpl`) is the bridge: it is a `Network::ReadFilter` that owns the HTTP `FilterManager`.\n\n---\n\n## File Reference Index\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.cc` | TCP `accept()` syscall, `onSocketEvent()` |\n| `source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc` | `onAccept()`, `onAcceptWorker()` |\n| `source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_socket.cc` | Listener filter iteration, `continueFilterChain()` |\n| `source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.cc` | `newConnection()`, server connection creation |\n| `source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.cc` | `findFilterChain()`, match criteria evaluation |\n| `source/common/network/filter_manager_impl.cc` | Network read/write filter iteration, `onRead()` |\n| `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` | HCM: `onData()`, `createCodec()`, `newStream()` |\n| `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` | HTTP filter chain iteration, `decodeHeaders()` |\n| `source/common/router/router.cc` | Route lookup, cluster selection, host selection, `createConnPool()` |\n| `source/common/router/upstream_request.cc` | `UpstreamRequest`, `acceptHeadersFromRouter()`, `conn_pool_->newStream()` |\n| `source/common/router/upstream_codec_filter.cc` | Terminal upstream filter, `encodeHeaders()` to codec, `CodecBridge` response path |\n| `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.cc` | `HttpConnPoolImplBase::newStream()`, `onPoolReady()` |\n| `source/common/http/conn_pool_base.h` | `Http::ActiveClient` constructor, `host()->createConnection()`, `createCodecClient()` |\n| `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc` | `tryCreateNewConnection()`, `attachStreamToClient()` |\n",
